alt="" class="bd ll mo c" width="700" height="350" loading="eager" role="presentation" src="https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:875/1*Vyd3ASj8w6CzzppwwA22SA.jpeg"></picture></div></div></figure><p id="8156" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Structural design patterns in Java play a crucial role in software development by focusing on class and object composition. They help in forming larger structures from individual parts, making the system more flexible and efficient. In this article, we’ll explore the key structural design patterns in Java, along with code examples for each.</p><h2 id="9eb0" class="nn no gr bb np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe of og oh oi oj ok bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">1. Adapter design pattern</h2><p id="9059" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Adapter Design Pattern <strong class="mr gs">allows objects with incompatible interfaces to collaborate.</strong> It acts as a bridge between two incompatible interfaces by converting the interface of one class into another interface that clients expect. This pattern is particularly useful when integrating new features or components into existing systems without modifying their source code.</p><h3 id="eef3" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Example</h3><p id="fbda" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Let’s consider a scenario where we have a MediaPlayer interface for playing audio files, but we want to extend its capabilities to play MP4 files as well. However, the MediaPlayer interface only supports playing MP3 files. We can use the Adapter pattern to bridge this gap.</p><h3 id="e391" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Implementation Steps</h3><p id="0ad4" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Before diving into the implementation, let’s outline the steps involved in creating an adapter:</p><ol class=""><li id="ad29" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Identify Incompatibilities:</strong> Determine the interfaces of the target and adaptee classes and identify the incompatibilities between them.</li><li id="c5d9" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Design the Adapter Interface:</strong> Design an interface that the client expects. This interface should provide a common ground for the client and the adaptee.</li><li id="85cb" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Create the Adapter Class: </strong>Implement the adapter class, which acts as a bridge between the client and the adaptee. The adapter class should implement the client’s interface and hold a reference to the adaptee.</li><li id="047c" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Implement the Adapter Logic:</strong> Implement the necessary logic inside the adapter class to convert calls from the client’s interface to the adaptee’s interface.</li></ol><h3 id="4d2c" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Example Implementation</h3><p id="ba6a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Let’s implement the AdapterPattern using the media player example:</p><p id="c014" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 1: Identify Incompatibilities</p><ul class=""><li id="3205" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Target Interface: MediaPlayer (supports playing MP3 files)</li><li id="e7a8" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Adaptee Interface: AdvancedMediaPlayer (supports playing MP4 files)</li></ul><p id="74df" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 2: Design the Adapter Interface</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="6dc7" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">interface</span> <span class="hljs-title">MediaPlayer</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">play</span>(<span class="hljs-params">String fileName</span>)</span>;<br>}</span></pre><p id="91e7" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 3: Create the Adapter Class</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="330f" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">MediaAdapter</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">MediaPlayer</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">AdvancedMediaPlayer</span> advancedMediaPlayer;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">MediaAdapter</span>(<span class="hljs-title.class">String</span> audioType) {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> (audioType.<span class="hljs-title.function">equalsIgnoreCase</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"mp4"</span>)) {<br>            advancedMediaPlayer = <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Mp4Player</span>();<br>        }<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">play</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">String</span> fileName</span>) {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> (fileName.<span class="hljs-title.function">endsWith</span>(<span class="hljs-string">".mp4"</span>)) {<br>            advancedMediaPlayer.<span class="hljs-title.function">playMp4</span>(fileName);<br>        }<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><p id="b98d" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 4: Implement the Adapter Logic</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="58a6" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">interface</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">AdvancedMediaPlayer</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">playMp4</span>(<span class="hljs-title.class">String</span> fileName);<br>}<br><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Mp4Player</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">AdvancedMediaPlayer</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">playMp4</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">String</span> fileName</span>) {<br>        <span class="hljs-title.class">System</span>.<span class="hljs-property">out</span>.<span class="hljs-title.function">println</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Playing MP4 file: "</span> + fileName);<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="eb56" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Usage</h3><p id="9e1e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s see how we can use the adapter in our client code:</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="f876" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Client</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">main</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">String</span>[] args</span>) {<br>        <span class="hljs-title.class">MediaPlayer</span> mediaPlayer = <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Mp3Player</span>();<br>        mediaPlayer.<span class="hljs-title.function">play</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"song.mp3"</span>); <span class="hljs-comment">// Plays MP3 file</span><br><br>        mediaPlayer = <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">MediaAdapter</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"mp4"</span>);<br>        mediaPlayer.<span class="hljs-title.function">play</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"movie.mp4"</span>); <span class="hljs-comment">// Plays MP4 file (via adapter)</span><br>    }<br>}</span></pre><p id="546c" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Adapter Design Pattern allows us to integrate incompatible interfaces by providing a bridge between them. By following the pre-implementation steps and designing the adapter class accordingly, we can seamlessly extend the functionality of existing systems without modifying their source code. This pattern promotes code reusability and flexibility in software design.</p><h2 id="d12b" class="nn no gr bb np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe of og oh oi oj ok bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">2. Bridge Design Pattern</h2><p id="1c59" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Bridge Pattern <strong class="mr gs">decouples an abstraction from its implementation, allowing both to vary independently.</strong> It provides a way to separate abstraction and implementation hierarchies, making the system more flexible and easier to maintain. In this article, we’ll explore the Bridge Pattern in Java with real-life examples and step-by-step implementation.</p><h3 id="139b" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="ah">Example:</strong></h3><p id="7bef" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Remote Control and Devices Imagine you have a remote control that can operate various devices such as TVs, DVD players, and stereos. Each device has its own set of functionalities (e.g., power on/off, volume control, channel selection). The remote control acts as an abstraction, while the devices represent different implementations. By decoupling the abstraction (remote control) from the implementation (devices), we can easily add new devices or change existing ones without modifying the remote control code.</p><h3 id="5be7" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Implementation Steps</h3><p id="21ed" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s walk through the steps involved in implementing the Bridge Pattern:</p><ol class=""><li id="1506" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Identify Abstraction and Implementation:</strong> Identify the abstraction and implementation hierarchies in your system. Abstraction represents the high-level functionality, while implementation represents the low-level details.</li><li id="f04c" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Define Abstraction and Implementation Interfaces:</strong> Define separate interfaces for abstraction and implementation. Abstraction should delegate the implementation to the implementation interface.</li><li id="3bf7" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Implement Abstraction and Implementations: </strong>Implement the abstraction and implementation interfaces. Abstraction should maintain a reference to the implementation interface and delegate the calls to it.</li><li id="a8a9" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Create Concrete Implementations:</strong> Create concrete implementations of the implementation interface. These implementations represent different variations or types of the implementation.</li></ol><h3 id="35ec" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Example Implementation</h3><p id="50bc" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Let’s implement the Bridge Pattern using the remote control and devices example:</p><p id="6b79" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 1: Identify Abstraction and Implementation</p><ul class=""><li id="a6fd" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Abstraction: RemoteControl</li><li id="82d7" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Implementation: Device</li></ul><p id="6a6e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 2: Define Abstraction and Implementation Interfaces</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="6c91" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Abstraction interface</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">interface</span> <span class="hljs-title">RemoteControl</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">powerOn</span>()</span>;<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">powerOff</span>()</span>;<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">setChannel</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> channel</span>)</span>;<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">volumeUp</span>()</span>;<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">volumeDown</span>()</span>;<br>}<br><br><span class="hljs-comment">// Implementation interface</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">interface</span> <span class="hljs-title">Device</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">powerOn</span>()</span>;<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">powerOff</span>()</span>;<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">setChannel</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> channel</span>)</span>;<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">volumeUp</span>()</span>;<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">volumeDown</span>()</span>;<br>}</span></pre><p id="32ad" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 3: Implement Abstraction and Implementations</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="bb4b" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Abstraction</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">abstract</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">AbstractRemoteControl</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">RemoteControl</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">protected</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Device</span> device;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">AbstractRemoteControl</span>(<span class="hljs-title.class">Device</span> device) {<br>        <span class="hljs-variable.language">this</span>.<span class="hljs-property">device</span> = device;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">powerOn</span>() {<br>        device.<span class="hljs-title.function">powerOn</span>();<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">powerOff</span>() {<br>        device.<span class="hljs-title.function">powerOff</span>();<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">setChannel</span>(<span class="hljs-params">int channel</span>) {<br>        device.<span class="hljs-title.function">setChannel</span>(channel);<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">volumeUp</span>() {<br>        device.<span class="hljs-title.function">volumeUp</span>();<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">volumeDown</span>() {<br>        device.<span class="hljs-title.function">volumeDown</span>();<br>    }<br>}<br><br><span class="hljs-comment">// Implementation</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">TV</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Device</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-comment">// Implementations for TV</span><br>}<br><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">DVDPlayer</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Device</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-comment">// Implementations for DVD player</span><br>}</span></pre><p id="2452" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 4: Create Concrete Implementations</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="95eb" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">SonyTV</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">extends</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">TV</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-comment">// Implementations specific to Sony TV</span><br>}<br><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">SamsungTV</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">extends</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">TV</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-comment">// Implementations specific to Samsung TV</span><br>}<br><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">PhilipsDVDPlayer</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">extends</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">DVDPlayer</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-comment">// Implementations specific to Philips DVD player</span><br>}</span></pre><h3 id="04ea" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Usage</h3><p id="93d7" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s see how we can use the Bridge Pattern in our client code:</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="a9be" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Client</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">main</span><span class="hljs-params">(String[] args)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-type">Device</span> <span class="hljs-variable">sonyTV</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">SonyTV</span>();<br>        <span class="hljs-type">RemoteControl</span> <span class="hljs-variable">remoteControl</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">ConcreteRemoteControl</span>(sonyTV);<br><br>        remoteControl.powerOn();<br>        remoteControl.setChannel(<span class="hljs-number">5</span>);<br>        remoteControl.volumeUp();<br><br>        <span class="hljs-type">Device</span> <span class="hljs-variable">philipsDVDPlayer</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">PhilipsDVDPlayer</span>();<br>        <span class="hljs-type">RemoteControl</span> <span class="hljs-variable">remoteControl2</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">ConcreteRemoteControl</span>(philipsDVDPlayer);<br><br>        remoteControl2.powerOn();<br>        remoteControl2.setChannel(<span class="hljs-number">3</span>);<br>        remoteControl2.volumeUp();<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><p id="f9be" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Bridge Pattern provides a way to separate abstraction from implementation, allowing both to vary independently. By following the implementation steps and designing abstraction and implementation hierarchies appropriately, we can achieve more flexible and maintainable software systems. In real-life scenarios, the Bridge Pattern is useful for managing complex hierarchies and handling variations in behavior or functionality.</p><h2 id="2660" class="nn no gr bb np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe of og oh oi oj ok bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">3. Composite Design Pattern</h2><p id="e6f5" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Composite Design Pattern <strong class="mr gs">allows you to compose objects into tree structures to represent part-whole hierarchies.</strong> It lets clients treat individual objects and compositions of objects uniformly. This pattern is useful when dealing with hierarchical structures where individual objects and compositions of objects need to be treated in the same way.</p><h3 id="152d" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="ah">Example</strong>:</h3><p id="25ce" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Organization Structure Consider an organization with a hierarchical structure consisting of departments, teams, and individual employees. Each department contains sub-departments, teams, and individual employees. The Composite Pattern can be used to represent this organizational structure, where each component (department, team, employee) behaves uniformly, allowing operations to be applied recursively.</p><h3 id="dc5c" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Implementation Steps</h3><p id="90df" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s walk through the steps involved in implementing the Composite Pattern:</p><ol class=""><li id="4d23" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Identify Component and Composite Classes:</strong> Identify the component interface and composite class(es) that will represent the hierarchy.</li><li id="5a2e" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Define Component Interface:</strong> Define an interface for the component classes, declaring common operations that can be performed on both individual objects and compositions.</li><li id="bf9b" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Implement Leaf and Composite Classes:</strong> Implement leaf classes for individual objects and composite classes for compositions of objects. Both leaf and composite classes should implement the component interface.</li><li id="ff53" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Implement Operations Recursively:</strong> Implement operations in the composite classes recursively, allowing them to be applied to both individual objects and compositions of objects.</li></ol><h3 id="02d3" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Example Implementation</h3><p id="f7b5" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Let’s implement the Composite Pattern using the organization structure example:</p><p id="b0ad" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 1: Identify Component and Composite Classes</p><ul class=""><li id="920d" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Component: Employee (interface)</li><li id="dc9c" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Composite: Department (composite class)</li></ul><p id="ad49" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 2: Define Component Interface</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="ee7a" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Component interface</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">interface</span> <span class="hljs-title">Employee</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">showDetails</span>()</span>;<br>}</span></pre><p id="9e41" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 3: Implement Leaf and Composite Classes</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="b838" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Leaf class</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Developer</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Employee</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">String</span> name;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Developer</span>(<span class="hljs-title.class">String</span> name) {<br>        <span class="hljs-variable.language">this</span>.<span class="hljs-property">name</span> = name;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">showDetails</span>() {<br>        <span class="hljs-title.class">System</span>.<span class="hljs-property">out</span>.<span class="hljs-title.function">println</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Developer: "</span> + name);<br>    }<br>}<br><br><span class="hljs-comment">// Composite class</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> java.<span class="hljs-property">util</span>.<span class="hljs-property">ArrayList</span>;<br><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> java.<span class="hljs-property">util</span>.<span class="hljs-property">List</span>;<br><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Department</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Employee</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">String</span> name;<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">List</span>&lt;<span class="hljs-title.class">Employee</span>&gt; employees = <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">ArrayList</span>&lt;&gt;();<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Department</span>(<span class="hljs-title.class">String</span> name) {<br>        <span class="hljs-variable.language">this</span>.<span class="hljs-property">name</span> = name;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">addEmployee</span>(<span class="hljs-params">Employee employee</span>) {<br>        employees.<span class="hljs-title.function">add</span>(employee);<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">showDetails</span>() {<br>        <span class="hljs-title.class">System</span>.<span class="hljs-property">out</span>.<span class="hljs-title.function">println</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Department: "</span> + name);<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> (<span class="hljs-title.class">Employee</span> employee : employees) {<br>            employee.<span class="hljs-title.function">showDetails</span>();<br>        }<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><p id="f475" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 4: Implement Operations Recursively</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="8a53" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">CompositePatternExample</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">main</span><span class="hljs-params">(String[] args)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-type">Employee</span> <span class="hljs-variable">dev1</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Developer</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"John"</span>);<br>        <span class="hljs-type">Employee</span> <span class="hljs-variable">dev2</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Developer</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Alice"</span>);<br><br>        <span class="hljs-type">Department</span> <span class="hljs-variable">engineering</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Department</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Engineering"</span>);<br>        engineering.addEmployee(dev1);<br>        engineering.addEmployee(dev2);<br><br>        <span class="hljs-type">Employee</span> <span class="hljs-variable">manager</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Manager</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Bob"</span>, engineering);<br><br>        manager.showDetails();<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="4e36" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Usage</h3><p id="607e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s see how we can use the Composite Pattern in our client code:</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="2301" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Client</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">main</span><span class="hljs-params">(String[] args)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-type">Employee</span> <span class="hljs-variable">dev1</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Developer</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"John"</span>);<br>        <span class="hljs-type">Employee</span> <span class="hljs-variable">dev2</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Developer</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Alice"</span>);<br><br>        <span class="hljs-type">Department</span> <span class="hljs-variable">engineering</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Department</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Engineering"</span>);<br>        engineering.addEmployee(dev1);<br>        engineering.addEmployee(dev2);<br><br>        <span class="hljs-type">Employee</span> <span class="hljs-variable">manager</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Manager</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Bob"</span>, engineering);<br><br>        manager.showDetails();<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><p id="1040" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Composite Design Pattern allows you to represent part-whole hierarchies in a unified way, treating individual objects and compositions of objects uniformly. By following the implementation steps and designing leaf and composite classes appropriately, we can create flexible and maintainable software systems. In real-life scenarios, the Composite Pattern is useful for representing hierarchical structures such as organization charts, file systems, and GUI components.</p><h2 id="a36c" class="nn no gr bb np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe of og oh oi oj ok bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">4. Decorator Design Pattern</h2><p id="efec" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Decorator Design Pattern is a structural pattern that allows behavior to be added to individual objects dynamically, without affecting the behavior of other objects from the same class. It is used to extend the functionality of objects in a flexible and reusable way by wrapping them with additional functionality at runtime. In this article, we’ll explore the Decorator Pattern in Java with a real-world example and step-by-step implementation.</p><h3 id="a4e0" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="ah">Example</strong>:</h3><p id="2fd4" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Coffee Ordering System Imagine you have a coffee ordering system where customers can order various types of coffee. Each coffee can have additional condiments such as milk, sugar, or whipped cream. The Decorator Pattern can be used to add these condiments dynamically to a base coffee object without modifying its class.</p><h3 id="2a2e" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Implementation Steps</h3><p id="e41e" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s walk through the steps involved in implementing the Decorator Pattern:</p><ol class=""><li id="2d78" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Identify Component and Decorator Classes:</strong> Identify the component interface and decorator classes that will extend its functionality.</li><li id="800b" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Define Component Interface:</strong> Define an interface for the component class, declaring the base operation(s) that all concrete components must implement.</li><li id="cfa5" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Implement Concrete Component:</strong> Implement a concrete component class that represents the base object to which additional functionality will be added.</li><li id="069d" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Implement Decorator Classes:</strong> Implement decorator classes that extend the functionality of the concrete component by adding additional behavior.</li><li id="26a4" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Use Decorators Dynamically:</strong> Use decorators to wrap concrete components dynamically at runtime, adding or removing functionality as needed.</li></ol><h3 id="6e1e" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Example Implementation</h3><p id="b403" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Let’s implement the Decorator Pattern using the coffee ordering system example:</p><div class="qe v"><div class="e"><a class="z ab ac fg af ag ah ai aj ak al am an ao ap v" rel="noopener follow" href="/download-app?source=promotion_paragraph---post_body_banner_surround_scribble--ebd2772d351f---------------------------------------"
