Identify Component and Decorator Classes</p><ul class=""><li id="a4d1" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Component: Coffee (interface)</li><li id="cfaf" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Decorators: MilkDecorator, SugarDecorator, WhippedCreamDecorator</li></ul><p id="31fc" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 2: Define Component Interface</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="7b92" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Component interface</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">interface</span> <span class="hljs-title">Coffee</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-built_in">double</span> <span class="hljs-title">cost</span>()</span>;<br>    <span class="hljs-function">String <span class="hljs-title">getDescription</span>()</span>;<br>}</span></pre><p id="7812" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 3: Implement Concrete Component</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="404b" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Concrete component</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">SimpleCoffee</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Coffee</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> double <span class="hljs-title.function">cost</span>() {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> <span class="hljs-number">2.0</span>; <span class="hljs-comment">// Base cost of simple coffee</span><br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">String</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">getDescription</span>() {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> <span class="hljs-string">"Simple coffee"</span>;<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><p id="0918" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 4: Implement Decorator Classes</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="3900" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Decorator classes</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">MilkDecorator</span> <span class="hljs-title">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title">Coffee</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> Coffee coffee;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-title">MilkDecorator</span>(<span class="hljs-params">Coffee coffee</span>)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">this</span>.coffee = coffee;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">double</span> <span class="hljs-title">cost</span>()</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> coffee.cost() + <span class="hljs-number">0.5</span>; <span class="hljs-comment">// Additional cost for milk</span><br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> String <span class="hljs-title">getDescription</span>()</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> coffee.getDescription() + <span class="hljs-string">", Milk"</span>;<br>    }<br>}<br><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">SugarDecorator</span> <span class="hljs-title">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title">Coffee</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> Coffee coffee;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-title">SugarDecorator</span>(<span class="hljs-params">Coffee coffee</span>)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">this</span>.coffee = coffee;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">double</span> <span class="hljs-title">cost</span>()</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> coffee.cost() + <span class="hljs-number">0.2</span>; <span class="hljs-comment">// Additional cost for sugar</span><br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> String <span class="hljs-title">getDescription</span>()</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> coffee.getDescription() + <span class="hljs-string">", Sugar"</span>;<br>    }<br>}<br><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">WhippedCreamDecorator</span> <span class="hljs-title">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title">Coffee</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> Coffee coffee;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-title">WhippedCreamDecorator</span>(<span class="hljs-params">Coffee coffee</span>)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">this</span>.coffee = coffee;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">double</span> <span class="hljs-title">cost</span>()</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> coffee.cost() + <span class="hljs-number">0.7</span>; <span class="hljs-comment">// Additional cost for whipped cream</span><br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> String <span class="hljs-title">getDescription</span>()</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> coffee.getDescription() + <span class="hljs-string">", Whipped Cream"</span>;<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="2779" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Usage</h3><p id="4f62" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s see how we can use the Decorator Pattern in our client code:</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="252a" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">Client</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">main</span>(<span class="hljs-params">String[] args</span>)</span> {<br>        Coffee simpleCoffee = <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> SimpleCoffee();<br>        System.<span class="hljs-keyword">out</span>.println(<span class="hljs-string">"Cost: $"</span> + simpleCoffee.cost() + <span class="hljs-string">", Description: "</span> + simpleCoffee.getDescription());<br><br>        Coffee coffeeWithMilkAndSugar = <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> MilkDecorator(<span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> SugarDecorator(<span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> SimpleCoffee()));<br>        System.<span class="hljs-keyword">out</span>.println(<span class="hljs-string">"Cost: $"</span> + coffeeWithMilkAndSugar.cost() + <span class="hljs-string">", Description: "</span> + coffeeWithMilkAndSugar.getDescription());<br><br>        Coffee coffeeWithWhippedCream = <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> WhippedCreamDecorator(<span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> SimpleCoffee());<br>        System.<span class="hljs-keyword">out</span>.println(<span class="hljs-string">"Cost: $"</span> + coffeeWithWhippedCream.cost() + <span class="hljs-string">", Description: "</span> + coffeeWithWhippedCream.getDescription());<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><p id="838d" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Decorator Design Pattern allows you to add behavior to objects dynamically, without modifying their class. By following the implementation steps and designing decorator classes appropriately, we can extend the functionality of objects in a flexible and reusable way. In real-world scenarios, the Decorator Pattern is useful for adding optional features or enhancements to objects, such as adding condiments to food items, customizing GUI components, or adding filters to streams.</p><h2 id="e39e" class="nn no gr bb np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe of og oh oi oj ok bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">5. Facade Design Pattern</h2><p id="97a6" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Facade Design Pattern <strong class="mr gs">provides a simplified interface to a set of interfaces in a subsystem.</strong> It hides the complexity of the subsystem and provides a unified interface to interact with it. This pattern promotes loose coupling between clients and the subsystem, making the system easier to use and maintain. In this article, we’ll explore the Facade Pattern in Java with real-world examples and step-by-step implementation.</p><h3 id="8e22" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="ah">Example</strong>:</h3><p id="3c24" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Home Theater System Imagine you have a complex home theater system consisting of multiple devices such as a DVD player, a television, a sound system, and more. Controlling each device individually can be cumbersome. The Facade Pattern can be used to create a simplified interface, such as a remote control, that hides the complexity of interacting with each device separately.</p><h3 id="d9d6" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Pre-Implementation Steps</h3><p id="1da2" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Before diving into the implementation, let’s outline the steps involved in creating a facade:</p><ol class=""><li id="74d6" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Identify Complex Subsystem: </strong>Identify the complex subsystem that needs to be simplified for clients.</li><li id="0a5e" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Design Facade Interface:</strong> Design an interface that provides a simplified view of the subsystem, hiding its complexity.</li><li id="3b18" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Implement Facade Class:</strong> Implement a facade class that encapsulates the interactions with the subsystem, providing methods to perform common tasks.</li><li id="e1f3" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Use Facade in Client Code: </strong>Use the facade interface in client code to interact with the subsystem, hiding its complexity.</li></ol><h3 id="73d2" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Example Implementation</h3><p id="603f" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Let’s implement the Facade Pattern using the home theater system example:</p><p id="9b8c" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 1: Identify Complex Subsystem</p><ul class=""><li id="e178" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Subsystem: HomeTheater (consisting of DVDPlayer, Television, SoundSystem, etc.)</li></ul><p id="7e3f" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 2: Design Facade Interface</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="21d4" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Facade interface</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">interface</span> <span class="hljs-title">HomeTheaterFacade</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">watchMovie</span>(<span class="hljs-params">String movie</span>)</span>;<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">endMovie</span>()</span>;<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">listenToMusic</span>()</span>;<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">stopMusic</span>()</span>;<br>}</span></pre><p id="ea47" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 3: Implement Facade Class</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="5c9a" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Facade class</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">HomeTheaterFacadeImpl</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">HomeTheaterFacade</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">DVDPlayer</span> dvdPlayer;<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Television</span> television;<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">SoundSystem</span> soundSystem;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">HomeTheaterFacadeImpl</span>(<span class="hljs-title.class">DVDPlayer</span> dvdPlayer, <span class="hljs-title.class">Television</span> television, <span class="hljs-title.class">SoundSystem</span> soundSystem) {<br>        <span class="hljs-variable.language">this</span>.<span class="hljs-property">dvdPlayer</span> = dvdPlayer;<br>        <span class="hljs-variable.language">this</span>.<span class="hljs-property">television</span> = television;<br>        <span class="hljs-variable.language">this</span>.<span class="hljs-property">soundSystem</span> = soundSystem;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">watchMovie</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">String</span> movie</span>) {<br>        dvdPlayer.<span class="hljs-title.function">turnOn</span>();<br>        dvdPlayer.<span class="hljs-title.function">play</span>(movie);<br>        television.<span class="hljs-title.function">turnOn</span>();<br>        television.<span class="hljs-title.function">setInput</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"DVD"</span>);<br>        soundSystem.<span class="hljs-title.function">turnOn</span>();<br>        soundSystem.<span class="hljs-title.function">setVolume</span>(<span class="hljs-number">10</span>);<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">endMovie</span>() {<br>        dvdPlayer.<span class="hljs-title.function">stop</span>();<br>        dvdPlayer.<span class="hljs-title.function">turnOff</span>();<br>        television.<span class="hljs-title.function">turnOff</span>();<br>        soundSystem.<span class="hljs-title.function">turnOff</span>();<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">listenToMusic</span>() {<br>        soundSystem.<span class="hljs-title.function">turnOn</span>();<br>        soundSystem.<span class="hljs-title.function">setVolume</span>(<span class="hljs-number">20</span>);<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">stopMusic</span>() {<br>        soundSystem.<span class="hljs-title.function">turnOff</span>();<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="8a90" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Usage</h3><p id="0687" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s see how we can use the Facade Pattern in our client code:</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="d389" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Client</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">main</span><span class="hljs-params">(String[] args)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-type">DVDPlayer</span> <span class="hljs-variable">dvdPlayer</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">DVDPlayer</span>();<br>        <span class="hljs-type">Television</span> <span class="hljs-variable">television</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Television</span>();<br>        <span class="hljs-type">SoundSystem</span> <span class="hljs-variable">soundSystem</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">SoundSystem</span>();<br><br>        <span class="hljs-type">HomeTheaterFacade</span> <span class="hljs-variable">facade</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">HomeTheaterFacadeImpl</span>(dvdPlayer, television, soundSystem);<br><br>        facade.watchMovie(<span class="hljs-string">"Inception"</span>);<br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Watching movie...</span><br><br>        facade.endMovie();<br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Movie ended...</span><br><br>        facade.listenToMusic();<br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Listening to music...</span><br><br>        facade.stopMusic();<br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Music stopped...</span><br>    }<br>}</span></pre><p id="6252" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Facade Design Pattern provides a simplified interface to a complex subsystem, making it easier to use and maintain. By encapsulating the interactions with the subsystem behind a facade, clients can interact with it without being exposed to its complexity. In real-world scenarios, the Facade Pattern is useful for simplifying interactions with complex systems such as APIs, frameworks, or libraries.</p><h2 id="890d" class="nn no gr bb np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe of og oh oi oj ok bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="ah">6. Flyweight Design Pattern</strong></h2><p id="ee4c" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Flyweight Design Pattern <strong class="mr gs">aims to minimize memory usage and improve performance by sharing object instances across multiple contexts.</strong> It achieves this by splitting the object state into intrinsic (shared) and extrinsic (context-dependent) parts. This pattern is particularly useful when dealing with a large number of similar objects that can share common state. In this article, we’ll delve into the Flyweight Pattern in Java with examples and step-by-step implementation.</p><p id="143a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Example</strong>: Text Editor Imagine you are developing a text editor application where users can create and edit documents. Each document may contain a large number of characters, and managing memory usage efficiently is crucial for performance. The Flyweight Pattern can be used to represent characters in the document, with shared instances for common characters such as letters, digits, and punctuation marks.</p><h3 id="2b81" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Implementation Steps</h3><p id="0e02" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s walk through the steps involved in implementing the Flyweight Pattern:</p><ol class=""><li id="efde" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Identify Common and Context-Dependent State:</strong> Identify the object state that can be shared (intrinsic state) and the state that varies across different contexts (extrinsic state).</li><li id="9268" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Design Flyweight Interface: </strong>Design an interface that declares methods to set and get the extrinsic state of the flyweight objects.</li><li id="1b49" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Implement Flyweight Class:</strong> Implement a flyweight class that represents the shared (intrinsic) state and provides methods to manipulate the extrinsic state.</li><li id="4fc2" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Create Factory for Flyweight Objects:</strong> Implement a factory class to create and manage flyweight objects, ensuring that shared instances are reused when possible.</li></ol><h3 id="1322" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Example Implementation</h3><p id="dd0a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Let’s implement the Flyweight Pattern using the text editor example:</p><p id="4623" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 1: Identify Common and Context-Dependent State</p><ul class=""><li id="a86b" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Common State: Character (e.g., ‘A’, ‘B’, ‘C’)</li><li id="5d8c" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Context-Dependent State: Position (x, y) in the document</li></ul><p id="ba72" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 2: Design Flyweight Interface</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="ec11" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Flyweight interface</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">interface</span> <span class="hljs-title">Character</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">display</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> positionX, <span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> positionY</span>)</span>;<br>}</span></pre><p id="9ceb" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 3: Implement Flyweight Class</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="098f" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Concrete flyweight class</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">ConcreteCharacter</span> <span class="hljs-title">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title">Character</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">char</span> character;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-title">ConcreteCharacter</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">char</span> character</span>)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">this</span>.character = character;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">display</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> positionX, <span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> positionY</span>)</span> {<br>        System.<span class="hljs-keyword">out</span>.println(<span class="hljs-string">"Character "</span> + character + <span class="hljs-string">" displayed at position ("</span> + positionX + <span class="hljs-string">", "</span> + positionY + <span class="hljs-string">")"</span>);<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><p id="5856" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 4: Create Factory for Flyweight Objects</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="719d" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Flyweight factory</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> java.util.HashMap;<br><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> java.util.Map;<br><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">CharacterFactory</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> Map&lt;Character, Character&gt; characterMap = <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">HashMap</span>&lt;&gt;();<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> Character <span class="hljs-title.function">getCharacter</span><span class="hljs-params">(<span class="hljs-type">char</span> key)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> (!characterMap.containsKey(key)) {<br>            characterMap.put(key, <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">ConcreteCharacter</span>(key));<br>        }<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> characterMap.get(key);<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="4d6e" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Usage</h3><p id="3065" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s see how we can use the Flyweight Pattern in our client code:</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="1a37" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Client</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">main</span><span class="hljs-params">(String[] args)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-type">CharacterFactory</span> <span class="hljs-variable">characterFactory</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">CharacterFactory</span>();<br><br>        <span class="hljs-type">Character</span> <span class="hljs-variable">characterA</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> characterFactory.getCharacter(<span class="hljs-string">'A'</span>);<br>        characterA.display(<span class="hljs-number">10</span>, <span class="hljs-number">20</span>);<br><br>        <span class="hljs-type">Character</span> <span class="hljs-variable">characterB</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> characterFactory.getCharacter(<span class="hljs-string">'B'</span>);<br>        characterB.display(<span class="hljs-number">30</span>, <span class="hljs-number">40</span>);<br><br>        <span class="hljs-type">Character</span> <span class="hljs-variable">characterA2</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> characterFactory.getCharacter(<span class="hljs-string">'A'</span>);<br>        characterA2.display(<span class="hljs-number">50</span>, <span class="hljs-number">60</span>);<br><br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Output:</span><br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Character A displayed at position (10, 20)</span><br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Character B displayed at position (30, 40)</span><br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Character A displayed at position (50, 60)</span><br>    }<br>}</span></pre><p id="a2bb" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Flyweight Design Pattern allows for efficient memory usage and improved performance by sharing common state across multiple objects. By separating intrinsic and extrinsic state and reusing shared instances, this pattern reduces memory footprint and enhances scalability. In real-world scenarios, the Flyweight Pattern is useful for optimizing applications that deal with a large number of similar objects, such as text processing, graphical user interfaces, and gaming environments.</p><h2 id="54d5" class="nn no gr bb np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe of og oh oi oj ok bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">7. Proxy Design Pattern</h2><p id="0db2" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Proxy Design Pattern<strong class="mr gs"> provides a surrogate or placeholder for another object to control access to it</strong>. It allows you to create a representative object that can act as a substitute for the real object. This pattern is useful for implementing lazy initialization, access control, logging, monitoring, and more. In this article, we’ll delve into the Proxy Pattern in Java with examples and step-by-step implementation.</p><p id="a970" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Example</strong>: Internet Access Control Imagine you are working in an organization where internet access needs to be controlled based on user privileges. A Proxy Pattern can be used to create a proxy object that checks the user’s privileges before granting access to certain websites. This proxy object acts as a surrogate for the real internet connection object and controls access to it.</p><h3 id="7fcb" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Implementation Steps</h3><p id="7e30" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s walk through the steps involved in implementing the Proxy Pattern:</p><ol class=""><li id="964e" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Identify Real Subject and Proxy Classes:</strong> Identify the real subject (object) and the proxy class that will act as a surrogate for the real subject.</li><li id="dce8" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Design Proxy Interface:</strong> Design an interface that declares methods to perform operations on the real subject.</li><li id="ef8c" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Implement Real Subject Class:</strong> Implement the real subject class that contains the actual business logic or functionality.</li><li id="4a6a" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm ph pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Implement Proxy Class:</strong> Implement the proxy class that wraps the real subject and controls access to it by intercepting requests.</li></ol><h3 id="6a47" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Example Implementation</h3><p id="eb9a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Let’s implement the Proxy Pattern using the internet access control example:</p><p id="2155" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 1: Identify Real Subject and Proxy Classes</p><ul class=""><li id="6a5e" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Real Subject: InternetConnection (interface)</li><li id="479a" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Proxy: InternetProxy (class)</li></ul><p id="6b01" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 2: Design Proxy Interface</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="e482" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Proxy interface</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">interface</span> <span class="hljs-title">InternetConnection</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">connect</span>(<span class="hljs-params">String website</span>)</span>;<br>}</span></pre><p id="390f" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 3: Implement Real Subject Class</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="79b9" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Real subject class</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">RealInternetConnection</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">InternetConnection</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">connect</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">String</span> website</span>) {<br>        <span class="hljs-title.class">System</span>.<span class="hljs-property">out</span>.<span class="hljs-title.function">println</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Connecting to website: "</span> + website);<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><p id="b8fb" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 4: Implement Proxy Class</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="cbb0" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-comment">// Proxy class</span><br><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">InternetProxy</span> <span class="hljs-title">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title">InternetConnection</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> RealInternetConnection realInternetConnection;<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> Set&lt;String&gt; allowedWebsites;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-title">InternetProxy</span>()</span> {<br>        realInternetConnection = <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> RealInternetConnection();<br>        allowedWebsites = <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> HashSet&lt;&gt;();<br>        allowedWebsites.<span class="hljs-keyword">add</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"example.com"</span>);<br>        allowedWebsites.<span class="hljs-keyword">add</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"google.com"</span>);<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">connect</span>(<span class="hljs-params">String website</span>)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> (allowedWebsites.contains(website)) {<br>            realInternetConnection.connect(website);<br>        } <span class="hljs-keyword">else</span> {<br>            System.<span class="hljs-keyword">out</span>.println(<span class="hljs-string">"Access to website "</span> + website + <span class="hljs-string">" is not allowed."</span>);<br>        }<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="a3f9" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Usage</h3><p id="694a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s see how we can use the Proxy Pattern in our client code:</p><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="4915" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Client</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">main</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">String</span>[] args</span>) {<br>        <span class="hljs-title.class">InternetConnection</span> internetConnection = <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">InternetProxy</span>();<br><br>        internetConnection.<span class="hljs-title.function">connect</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"example.com"</span>); <span class="hljs-comment">// Allowed</span><br>        internetConnection.<span class="hljs-title.function">connect</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"google.com"</span>); <span class="hljs-comment">// Allowed</span><br>        internetConnection.<span class="hljs-title.function">connect</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"facebook.com"</span>); <span class="hljs-comment">// Not allowed</span><br>    }<br>}</span></pre><p id="c6a2" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Proxy Design Pattern provides a surrogate or placeholder for another object to control access to it. By separating the proxy from the real subject, this pattern enables additional functionality such as access control, logging, and monitoring. In real-world scenarios, the Proxy Pattern is useful for implementing lazy initialization, remote access, caching, and more.</p><h2 id="08ac" class="nn no gr bb np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe of og oh oi oj ok bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="ah">Conclusion:</strong></h2><p id="f467" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">structural design patterns in Java are powerful tools that enable developers to create flexible, maintainable, and scalable software architectures. These patterns focus on organizing classes and objects in a way that promotes reusability, enhances flexibility, and simplifies complex systems. By encapsulating common design structures and principles, structural patterns provide clear guidelines and best practices for designing robust software solutions.</p><p id="2c37" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Throughout this exploration of structural design patterns, we’ve seen how patterns like the Adapter, Bridge, Composite, Decorator, Facade, and Proxy can address various design challenges and improve the overall quality of software systems. Whether it’s integrating disparate interfaces, managing hierarchical structures, extending object functionality, simplifying complex subsystems, controlling access to objects, or optimizing performance, structural patterns offer practical solutions that can be applied to a wide range of real-world scenarios.</p><p id="b909" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">As developers, understanding and applying structural design patterns empowers us to design more elegant, efficient, and maintainable Java applications. By leveraging these patterns effectively, we can create software architectures that are not only resilient to change but also adaptable to evolving requirements and scalable for future growth.</p><p id="659c" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">In essence, structural design patterns serve as a blueprint for building software systems that are not only functional but also well-organized, extensible, and easy to maintain. They represent best practices distilled from years of collective experience in software engineering, offering valuable insights into how to design software systems that stand the test of time. With a solid understanding of structural design patterns and their applications, developers can elevate the quality and craftsmanship of their Java projects, ultimately delivering better outcomes for users and stakeholders alike.</p></div>

role="tooltip"><div tabindex="-1" class="ba"><p class="bb b ec u eb"><button class="z ab ac fg af ag ah ai aj ak al am an ao ap vr ti">607<span class="e au ra rb rc rd"></span></button></p></div></div></div></div></div></div><div><div class="bi" aria-describedby="1244" aria-labelledby="1244" role="tooltip"><div tabindex="-1" class="ba"><button class="ak kd kw kx v j ef ky kz" aria-label="responses"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" class="kv"><path d="M18.006 16.803c1.533-1.456 2.234-3.325 2.234-5.321C20.24 7.357 16.709 4 12.191 4S4 7.357 4 11.482c0 4.126 3.674 7.482 8.191 7.482.817 0 1.622-.111 2.393-.327.231.2.48.391.744.559 1.06.693 2.203 1.044 3.399 1.044.224-.008.4-.112.486-.287a.49.49 0 0 0-.042-.518c-.495-.67-.845-1.364-1.04-2.057a4 4 0 0 1-.125-.598zm-3.122 1.055-.067-.223-.315.096a8 8 0 0 1-2.311.338c-4.023 0-7.292-2.955-7.292-6.587 0-3.633 3.269-6.588 7.292-6.588 4.014 0 7.112 2.958 7.112 6.593 0 1.794-.608 3.469-2.027 4.72l-.195.168v.255c0 .056 0 .151.016.295.025.231.081.478.154.733.154.558.398 1.117.722 1.659a5.3 5.3 0 0 1-2.165-.845c-.276-.176-.714-.383-.941-.59z"></path></svg><p class="bb b ec u eb"><span class="pw-responses-count ku kv">3</span></p></button></div></div></div></div><div class="v j jh ji jj jk jl jm jn jo jp jq jr js jt ju jv"><div class="la bt by r s"></div><div class="au bt"><div><div class="bi" aria-describedby="1245" aria-labelledby="1245" role="tooltip"><div tabindex="-1" class="ba"><div class="bi"><button aria-controls="addToCatalogBookmarkButton" aria-expanded="false" aria-label="Add to list bookmark button" data-testid="headerBookmarkButton" class="z ef ac fg af ag ah lb aj ak al eg lc ld le"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 24 24" class="ar"><path fill="#000" d="M17.5 1.25a.5.5 0 0 1 1 0v2.5H21a.5.5 0 0 1 0 0 0 0-.6 0l-5.2 4z"></path></svg></button></div></div></div></div></div><div class="fq lf cr"><div class="e y"><div class="v cf"><div class="lg lh li lj lk ll cm bd"><div class="v"><div><a class="z ab class="ba"><button aria-label="More options" data-testid="headerStoryOptionsButton" class="z ef ac fg af ag ah lb aj ak al eg eh ei kz lm ln lo lp lq l lr ls lt lu lv lw lx n ly lz ma"><svg 1.42-.59.58-.86.58-1.41-.2-1.02-.58-1.41a1.93 1.93 0 0 0-1.42-.59c-.56 0-1.04.2-1.43.59s-.58.86-.58 1.41" clip-rule="evenodd"></path></svg><div class="by r s"><p class="bb b bc u eb">More</p></div></button></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><figure class="me mf mg mh mi mj mb mc paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="mk ml ej mm href="https://unsplash.com/?utm_source=medium&amp;utm_medium=referral" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Unsplash</a></figcaption></figure><p id="5fd1" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Behavioral design patterns in Java are a category of design patterns that address<strong class="mr gs"> how objects communicate and interact with each other</strong>. They focus on defining algorithms and assignment of responsibilities between objects in a system. These patterns emphasize the delegation of behaviors between objects and aim to improve the flexibility and maintainability of the codebase. In this article, we’ll learn type of behavioral design patterns in Java, along with examples for each type.</p><h2 id="cf84" class="nn no gr bb np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe of og oh oi oj ok bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">1. Observer Pattern</h2><p id="8c8f" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Observer pattern defines <strong class="mr gs">a one-to-many dependency between objects so that when one object changes state, all its dependents are notified and updated automatically.</strong> This pattern is widely used in event handling systems. This allows for a loosely coupled design where subjects (observed objects) and observers (dependent objects) can interact without having explicit knowledge of each other.</p><p id="47c0" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Let’s consider a real-time example of a stock market monitoring system to understand the Observer pattern in action. In this scenario:</p><ul class=""><li id="5fd9" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Subject (Observable):</strong> The stock market is the subject. It maintains a list of observers (investors) interested in receiving updates about stock prices.</li><li id="e564" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Observer (Subscriber):</strong> Investors who want to receive updates about specific stocks are the observers. They subscribe to receive notifications about price changes.</li></ul><h2 id="e256" class="nn no gr bb np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe of og oh oi oj ok bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Implementation Steps</h2><p id="d579" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s walk through the steps to implement the Observer pattern for the stock market monitoring system in Java:</p><h3 id="b3cd" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 1: Define the Subject Interface</h3><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="3df3" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> java.util.List;<br><br><span class="hljs-keyword">interface</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Subject</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">registerObserver</span><span class="hljs-params">(Observer observer)</span>;<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">removeObserver</span><span class="hljs-params">(Observer observer)</span>;<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">notifyObservers</span><span class="hljs-params">()</span>;<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="aed5" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 2: Implement the Subject</h3><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="9ed8" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> java.util.ArrayList;<br><span class="hljs-keyword">import</span> java.util.List;<br><br><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">StockMarket</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Subject</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> List&lt;Observer&gt; observers = <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">ArrayList</span>&lt;&gt;();<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> String stockName;<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> <span class="hljs-type">double</span> price;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">setStockData</span><span class="hljs-params">(String stockName, <span class="hljs-type">double</span> price)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-built_in">this</span>.stockName = stockName;<br>        <span class="hljs-built_in">this</span>.price = price;<br>        notifyObservers();<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-meta">@Override</span><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">registerObserver</span><span class="hljs-params">(Observer observer)</span> {<br>        observers.add(observer);<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-meta">@Override</span><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">removeObserver</span><span class="hljs-params">(Observer observer)</span> {<br>        observers.remove(observer);<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-meta">@Override</span><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">notifyObservers</span><span class="hljs-params">()</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">for</span> (Observer observer : observers) {<br>            observer.update(stockName, price);<br>        }<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="66a9" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 3: Define the Observer Interface</h3><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="569e" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">interface</span> <span class="hljs-title">Observer</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">update</span>(<span class="hljs-params">String stockName, <span class="hljs-built_in">double</span> price</span>)</span>;<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="b742" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 4: Implement the Observer</h3><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="e232" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Investor</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Observer</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">String</span> name;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Investor</span>(<span class="hljs-title.class">String</span> name) {<br>        <span class="hljs-variable.language">this</span>.<span class="hljs-property">name</span> = name;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-meta">@Override</span><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">update</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">String</span> stockName, double price</span>) {<br>        <span class="hljs-title.class">System</span>.<span class="hljs-property">out</span>.<span class="hljs-title.function">println</span>(name + <span class="hljs-string">" received update: "</span> + stockName + <span class="hljs-string">" price is now $"</span> + price);<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="b5bf" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 5: Test the Implementation</h3><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="34bd" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Main</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">main</span><span class="hljs-params">(String[] args)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-type">StockMarket</span> <span class="hljs-variable">stockMarket</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">StockMarket</span>();<br><br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Create observers (investors)</span><br>        <span class="hljs-type">Investor</span> <span class="hljs-variable">investor1</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Investor</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"John"</span>);<br>        <span class="hljs-type">Investor</span> <span class="hljs-variable">investor2</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Investor</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Alice"</span>);<br><br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Register observers</span><br>        stockMarket.registerObserver(investor1);<br>        stockMarket.registerObserver(investor2);<br><br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Set stock data (trigger notification)</span><br>        stockMarket.setStockData(<span class="hljs-string">"ABC"</span>, <span class="hljs-number">100.0</span>);<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><p id="272a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">By implementing the Observer pattern, we achieved a loosely coupled design where the stock market (subject) notifies its investors (observers) about changes in stock prices. This pattern promotes flexibility and extensibility by allowing new observers to be added without modifying existing code, making it a valuable tool for building reactive and scalable systems.</p><h2 id="a178" class="nn no gr bb np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe of og oh oi oj ok bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">2. Strategy Design Pattern</h2><p id="4ca7" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Strategy design pattern <strong class="mr gs">allows an algorithm’s behavior to be selected at runtime. </strong>It defines a family of algorithms, encapsulates each one, and makes them interchangeable. This pattern enables the algorithm to vary independently of the clients that use it, promoting flexibility and ease of maintenance.</p><p id="db25" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Let’s consider a real-time example of a payment processing system to understand the Strategy pattern in action. In this scenario:</p><ul class=""><li id="5fc9" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Context:</strong> The payment processing system acts as the context. It interacts with different payment gateways to process payments.</li><li id="6410" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Strategy:</strong> Each payment gateway (e.g., PayPal, Stripe, Square) represents a strategy. Each strategy encapsulates the algorithm for processing payments.</li></ul><h2 id="546a" class="nn no gr bb np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe of og oh oi oj ok bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Implementation Steps</h2><p id="bf6b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s walk through the steps to implement the Strategy pattern for the payment processing system in Java:</p><h3 id="b111" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 1: Define the PaymentStrategy Interface</h3><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="b47a" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">interface</span> <span class="hljs-title">PaymentStrategy</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">processPayment</span>(<span class="hljs-params"><span class="hljs-built_in">double</span> amount</span>)</span>;<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="decd" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 2: Implement Concrete Payment Strategies</h3><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="228a" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span        <span class="hljs-variable.language">this</span>.<span class="hljs-property">email</span> = email;<br>        <span class="hljs-variable.language">this</span>.<span <span class="hljs-title.class">System</span>.<span class="hljs-property">out</span>.<span class="hljs-title.function">println</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Payment processed via PayPal: $"</span> class="hljs-variable.language">this</span>.<span class="hljs-property">apiKey</span> = apiKey;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-meta">@Override</span><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">processPayment</span>(<span class="hljs-params">double amount</span>) {<br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Process payment using Stripe API</span><br>        <span class="hljs-title.class">System</span>.<span class="hljs-property">out</span>.<span class="hljs-title.function">println</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"Payment processed via Stripe: $"</span> + amount);<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="c483" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 3: Define the PaymentContext</h3><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="90af" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">PaymentContext</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> PaymentStrategy paymentStrategy;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-title">PaymentContext</span><span class="hljs-params">(PaymentStrategy paymentStrategy)</span> </span>{<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">this</span>.paymentStrategy = paymentStrategy;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-type">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">setPaymentStrategy</span><span class="hljs-params">(PaymentStrategy paymentStrategy)</span> </span>{<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">this</span>.paymentStrategy = paymentStrategy;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-type">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">processPayment</span><span class="hljs-params">(<span class="hljs-type">double</span> amount)</span> </span>{<br>        paymentStrategy.<span class="hljs-built_in">processPayment</span>(amount);<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="ce19" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 4: Test the Implementation</h3><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="4502" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Main</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">main</span><span class="hljs-params">(String[] args)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Create payment context with PayPal strategy</span><br>        <span class="hljs-type">PaymentStrategy</span> <span class="hljs-variable">paypalStrategy</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">PayPalStrategy</span>(<span class="hljs-string">"paypal@example.com"</span>, <span class="hljs-string">"password"</span>);<br>        <span class="hljs-type">PaymentContext</span> <span class="hljs-variable">paymentContext</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">PaymentContext</span>(paypalStrategy);<br><br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Process payment using PayPal</span><br>        paymentContext.processPayment(<span class="hljs-number">100.0</span>);<br><br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Switch to Stripe strategy</span><br>        <span class="hljs-type">PaymentStrategy</span> <span class="hljs-variable">stripeStrategy</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span paymentContext.setPaymentStrategy(stripeStrategy);<br><br>        <span class="hljs-comment">// Process payment using Stripe</span><br>        paymentContext.processPayment(<span class="hljs-number">150.0</span>);<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><p id="6732" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">By implementing the Strategy pattern, we achieved a flexible and extensible solution where the payment processing algorithm can be dynamically selected at runtime. This pattern promotes code reuse, maintainability, and scalability by encapsulating algorithms into interchangeable components. Understanding and applying the Strategy pattern can greatly enhance the design and architecture of software systems, especially those with varying requirements for algorithmic behavior.</p><h2 id="db48" class="nn no gr bb np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe of og oh oi oj ok bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">3. Chain of Responsibility Pattern</h2><p id="537c" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">The Chain of Responsibility pattern <strong class="mr gs">allows an object to pass a request along a chain of handlers. </strong>Each handler in the chain decides either to process the request or to pass it to the next handler in the chain. This pattern decouples senders and receivers of requests, giving multiple objects the opportunity to handle the request.</p><p id="2468" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Let’s consider a real-time example of an employee leave approval system to understand the Chain of Responsibility pattern in action. In this scenario:</p><ul class=""><li id="688f" class="mp mq gr mr b ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Request:</strong> Employee leave requests are initiated by employees and need to be approved by different levels of management: team leads, managers, and department heads.</li><li id="79c9" class="mp mq gr mr b ms pk mu mv mw pl my mz na pm nc nd ne pn ng nh ni po nk nl nm pp pi pj bg" data-selectable-paragraph=""><strong class="mr gs">Handlers:</strong> Each level of management represents a handler in the chain. If a handler can’t approve the leave request, it passes the request to the next higher level in the management hierarchy.</li></ul><h2 id="5696" class="nn no gr bb np nq nr ns nt nu nv nw nx ny nz oa ob oc od oe of og oh oi oj ok bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Implementation Steps</h2><p id="9aef" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mp mq gr mr b ms ol mu mv mw om my mz na on nc nd ne oo ng nh ni op nk nl nm gk bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Now, let’s walk through the steps to implement the Chain of Responsibility pattern for the employee leave approval system in Java:</p><h3 id="df6d" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 1: Define the Request Class</h3><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="048c" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title">LeaveRequest</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> String employeeName;<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> days;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span <span class="hljs-keyword">this</span>.employeeName = employeeName;<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">this</span>.days = days;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> String <span class="hljs-title">getEmployeeName</span>()</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> employeeName;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">int</span> <span class="hljs-title">getDays</span>()</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> days;<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="4280" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 2: Define the Handler Interface</h3><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="574f" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">interface</span> <span class="hljs-title">LeaveApprover</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title">approveLeave</span>(<span class="hljs-params">LeaveRequest leaveRequest</span>)</span>;<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="4751" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 3: Implement Concrete Handlers</h3><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="c97a" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">TeamLead</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">LeaveApprover</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">final</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">setNextApprover</span><span class="hljs-params">(LeaveApprover nextApprover)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-built_in">this</span>.nextApprover = nextApprover;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-meta">@Override</span><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">approveLeave</span><span class="hljs-params">(LeaveRequest leaveRequest)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> (leaveRequest.getDays() &lt;= MAX_LEAVES_ALLOWED) {<br>            System.out.println(<span class="hljs-string">"Leave approved by Team Lead for "</span> + leaveRequest.getEmployeeName());<br>        } <span class="hljs-keyword">else</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> (nextApprover != <span class="hljs-literal">null</span>) {<br>            nextApprover.approveLeave(leaveRequest);<br>        }<br>    }<br>}<br><br><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">Manager</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">LeaveApprover</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">final</span> <span class="hljs-type">int</span> <span class="hljs-variable">MAX_LEAVES_ALLOWED</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-number">5</span>;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> LeaveApprover nextApprover;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">setNextApprover</span><span class="hljs-params">(LeaveApprover nextApprover)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-built_in">this</span>.nextApprover = nextApprover;<br>    }<br><br>    <span class="hljs-meta">@Override</span><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span (leaveRequest.getDays() &lt;= MAX_LEAVES_ALLOWED) {<br>            System.out.println(<span class="hljs-string">"Leave approved by Manager for "</span> + leaveRequest.getEmployeeName());<br>        } <span class="hljs-keyword">else</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> (nextApprover != <span class="hljs-literal">null</span>) {<br>            nextApprover.approveLeave(leaveRequest);<br>        }<br>    }<br>}<br><br><span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">DepartmentHead</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">implements</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">LeaveApprover</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">private</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">final</span> <span class="hljs-type">int</span> <span class="hljs-variable">MAX_LEAVES_ALLOWED</span> <span class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-number">10</span>;<br><br>    <span class="hljs-meta">@Override</span><br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">approveLeave</span><span class="hljs-params">(LeaveRequest leaveRequest)</span> {<br>        <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> (leaveRequest.getDays() &lt;= MAX_LEAVES_ALLOWED) {<br>            System.out.println(<span class="hljs-string">"Leave approved by Department Head for "</span> + leaveRequest.getEmployeeName());<br>        } <span class="hljs-keyword">else</span> {<br>            System.out.println(<span class="hljs-string">"Leave denied for "</span> + leaveRequest.getEmployeeName());<br>        }<br>    }<br>}</span></pre><h3 id="1925" class="oq no gr bb np or os ot nt ou ov ow nx na ox oy oz ne pa pb pc ni pd pe pf pg bg" data-selectable-paragraph="">Step 4: Construct the Chain</h3><pre class="pq pr ps pt pu pv pw px bl py ax bg"><span id="5324" class="pz no gr pw b bc qa qb e qc qd" data-selectable-paragraph=""><span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">class</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">ChainOfResponsibilityExample</span> {<br>    <span class="hljs-keyword">public</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">static</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">void</span> <span class="hljs-title.function">main</span><span class="hljs-params">(String[] class="hljs-operator">=</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-title.class">TeamLead</span>();<br>        <span class="hljs-type">Manager</span> <span
